class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="mw-head-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t\t\t<a id="top"></a>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n\t\t\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Emergency management</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Disaster_preparedness&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Disaster preparedness">Disaster preparedness</a>)</span></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">\n\t\t\t\t\tJump to:\t\t\t\t\t<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, \t\t\t\t\t<a href="#p-search">search</a>\n\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p><b>Emergency management</b> is the organization and management of resources and responsibilities for dealing with all humanitarian aspects of emergencies\xe2\x80\x94preparedness, response, and recovery\xe2\x80\x94in order to reduce the harmful effects of all hazards, including disasters. Often interchanged with disaster management, it is not be confused with it. The World Health Organization defines an emergency as the state in which normal procedures are interrupted, and immediate measures need to be taken to prevent that state turning into a disaster. Thus, emergency management is crucial to avoid the disruption transforming into a disaster, which is harder to recover from.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a risks</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergency_planning_ideals">Emergency planning ideals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Emergency planning ideals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(March 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>If possible, emergency planning should aim to prevent emergencies from occurring, and failing that, should develop a good action plan to mitigate the results and effects of any emergencies. As time goes on, and more data becomes available, usually through the study of emergencies as they occur, a plan should evolve. The development of emergency plans is a cyclical process, common to many risk management disciplines, such as Business Continuity and Security Risk Management, as set out below:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Recognition or identification of risks</li>\n<li>Ranking or evaluation of risks</li>\n<li>Responding to significant risks</li>\n<li>Tolerate</li>\n<li>Treat</li>\n<li>Transfer</li>\n<li>Terminate</li>\n<li>Resourcing controls and planning</li>\n<li>Reaction Planning</li>\n<li>Reporting &amp; monitoring risk performance</li>\n<li>Reviewing the Risk Management framework</li>\n</ul>\n<p>There are a number of guidelines and publications regarding Emergency Planning, published by various professional organizations such as ASIS, National Fire Protection Association (NFPA), and the International Association of Emergency Managers (IAEM). There are very few Emergency Management specific standards, and emergency management as a discipline tends to fall under business resilience standards.</p>\n<p>In order to avoid, or reduce significant losses to a business, emergency managers should work to identify and anticipate potential risks, hopefully to reduce their probability of occurring. In the event that an emergency does occur, managers should have a plan prepared to mitigate the effects of that emergency, as well as to ensure Business Continuity of critical operations post-incident. It is essential for an organisation to include procedures for determining whether an emergency situation has occurred and at what point an emergency management plan should be activated.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Implementation_ideals">Implementation ideals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Implementation ideals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(March 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>An emergency plan must be regularly maintained, in a structured and methodical manner, to ensure it is up-to-date in the event of an emergency. Emergency managers generally follow a common process to anticipate, assess, prevent, prepare, respond and recover from an incident.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-incident_training_and_testing">Pre-incident training and testing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-incident training and testing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emergency_Responders_(8743399305).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Emergency_Responders_%288743399305%29.jpg/220px-Emergency_Responders_%288743399305%29.jpg" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Emergency_Responders_%288743399305%29.jpg/330px-Emergency_Responders_%288743399305%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Emergency_Responders_%288743399305%29.jpg/440px-Emergency_Responders_%288743399305%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2655" data-file-height="2276" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emergency_Responders_(8743399305).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA team of emergency responders performs a training scenario involving <a href="/wiki/Anthrax" title="Anthrax">anthrax</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Emergency management plans and procedures should include the identification of appropriately trained staff members responsible for decision-making when an emergency occurs. Training plans should include internal people, contractors and civil protection partners, and should state the nature and frequency of training and testing.</p>\n<p>Testing of a plan\'s effectiveness should occur regularly. In instances where several business or organisations occupy the same space, joint emergency plans, formally agreed to by all parties, should be put into place.</p>\n<p>Drills and exercises in preparation for foreseeable hazards are often held, with the participation of the services that will be involved in handling the emergency, and people who will be affected. Drills are held to prepare for the hazards of <a href="/wiki/Fire_drill" title="Fire drill">fires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tornado_drill" class="mw-redirect" title="Tornado drill">tornadoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lockdown" title="Lockdown">lockdown</a> for protection, <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">earthquakes</a>, etc.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communicating_and_incident_assessment">Communicating and incident assessment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Communicating and incident assessment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Communication is one of the key issues during any emergency, pre-planning of communications is critical. Miscommunication can easily result in emergency events escalating unnecessarily.</p>\n<p>Once an emergency has been identified a comprehensive assessment evaluating the level of impact and its financial implications should be undertaken. Following assessment, the appropriate plan or response to be activated will depend on a specific pre-set criteria within the emergency plan. The steps necessary should be prioritized to ensure critical functions are operational as soon as possible. The critical functions are those that makes the plan untenable if not operationalized.</p>\n<p>The Communication policy must be well known and rehearsed and all targeted audiences or publics and individuals must be alert. All Communication infrastructure must be as prepared as possible with all information on groupings clearly identified.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phases_and_personal_activities">Phases and personal activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Phases and personal activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(March 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Emergency management consists of five phases: prevention, mitigation, preparedness, response and recovery. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.fema.gov/mission-areas">http://www.fema.gov/mission-areas</a></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prevention">Prevention</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Prevention">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>It focuses on preventing the human hazard, primarily from potential natural disasters or terrorist attacks. Preventive measures are taken on both the domestic and international levels, designed to provide permanent protection from disasters. also by doing this the risk of loss of life and injury can be mitigated with good evacuation plans, environmental planning and design standards. In January 2005, 167 Governments adopted a 10-year global plan for natural disaster risk reduction called the <a href="/wiki/World_Conference_on_Disaster_Risk_Reduction" title="World Conference on Disaster Risk Reduction">Hyogo Framework</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<p>Preventing or reducing the impacts of disasters on our communities is a key focus for emergency management efforts today. Prevention and mitigation also help reduce the financial costs of disaster response and recovery. Public Safety Canada is working with provincial and territorial governments and stakeholders to promote disaster prevention and mitigation using a risk-based and all-hazards approach. In 2009, Federal/Provincial/Territorial Ministers endorsed a National Disaster Mitigation Strategy.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mitigation">Mitigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mitigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Disaster mitigation measures are those that eliminate or reduce the impacts and risks of hazards through proactive measures taken before an emergency or disaster occurs.</p>\n<p>Preventive or mitigation measures take different forms for different types of disasters. In earthquake prone areas, these preventive measures might include structural changes such as the installation of an <a href="/wiki/Earthquake_valve" title="Earthquake valve">earthquake valve</a> to instantly shut off the natural gas supply, <a href="/wiki/Seismic_retrofit" title="Seismic retrofit">seismic retrofits</a> of property, and the securing of items inside a building. The latter may include the mounting of furniture, <a href="/wiki/Refrigerator" title="Refrigerator">refrigerators</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_heater" class="mw-redirect" title="Water heater">water heaters</a> and breakables to the walls, and the addition of cabinet latches. In flood prone areas, houses can be built on poles/stilts. In areas prone to prolonged electricity <a href="/wiki/Power_blackout" class="mw-redirect" title="Power blackout">black-outs</a> installation of a <a href="/wiki/Electrical_generator" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical generator">generator</a> ensures continuation of electrical service. The construction of <a href="/wiki/Storm_cellar" title="Storm cellar">storm cellars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fallout_shelter" title="Fallout shelter">fallout shelters</a> are further examples of personal mitigative actions.</p>\n<p>On a national level, governments might implement large scale mitigation measures. After the monsoon floods of 2010, the Punjab government subsequently constructed 22 \'disaster-resilient\' model villages, comprising 1885 single-storey homes, together with schools and health centres.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<p>One of the best known examples of investment in disaster mitigation is the Red River Floodway. The building of the Floodway was a joint provincial/federal undertaking to protect the City of Winnipeg and reduce the impact of flooding in the Red River Basin. It cost $62.7 million to build in the 1960s. Since then, the floodway has been used over 20 times. Its use during the 1997 Red River Flood alone saved an estimated $4.5 billion in costs from potential damage to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The Floodway was expanded in 2006 as a joint provincial/federal initiative.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparedness">Preparedness</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Preparedness">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Panther_8x8_action_15x10.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Panther_8x8_action_15x10.jpg/220px-Panther_8x8_action_15x10.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Panther_8x8_action_15x10.jpg/330px-Panther_8x8_action_15x10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Panther_8x8_action_15x10.jpg/440px-Panther_8x8_action_15x10.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1772" data-file-height="1181" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panther_8x8_action_15x10.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAn airport emergency preparedness exercise</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Preparedness focuses on preparing equipment and procedures for use when a <a href="/wiki/Disaster" title="Disaster">disaster</a> occurs. This equipment and these procedures can be used to reduce vulnerability to disaster, to mitigate the impacts of a disaster or to respond more efficiently in an <a href="/wiki/Emergency" title="Emergency">emergency</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA) has set out a basic four-stage vision of preparedness flowing from mitigation to preparedness to response to recovery and back to mitigation in a circular planning process.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> This circular, overlapping model has been modified by other agencies, taught in emergency class and discussed in academic papers.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>\n<p>FEMA also operates a Building Science Branch that develops and produces multi-hazard mitigation guidance that focuses on creating disaster-resilient communities to reduce loss of life and property.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> FEMA advises citizens to prepare their homes with some emergency essentials in the case that the food distribution lines are interrupted. FEMA has subsequently prepared for this contingency by purchasing hundreds of thousands of freeze dried food emergency meals ready to eat (MRE\'s) to dispense to the communities where emergency shelter and evacuations are implemented.</p>\n<p>Some guidelines for household preparedness have been put online by the State of Colorado, on the topics of water, food, tools, and so on.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Emergency preparedness can be difficult to measure.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> CDC focuses on evaluating the effectiveness of its public health efforts through a variety of measurement and assessment programs.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_Emergency_Planning_Committees">Local Emergency Planning Committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Local Emergency Planning Committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Local_Emergency_Planning_Committee" title="Local Emergency Planning Committee">Local Emergency Planning Committees</a> (LEPCs) are required by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">United States Environmental Protection Agency</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Planning_and_Community_Right-to-Know_Act" title="Emergency Planning and Community Right-to-Know Act">Emergency Planning and Community Right-to-Know Act</a> to develop an emergency response plan, review the plan at least annually, and provide information about chemicals in the community to local citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> This emergency preparedness effort focuses on hazards presented by use and storage of extremely hazardous and toxic chemicals.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Particular requirements of LEPCs include</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Identification of facilities and transportation routes of extremely hazardous substances</li>\n<li>Description of emergency response procedures, on and off site</li>\n<li>Designation of a community coordinator and facility emergency coordinator(s) to implement the plan</li>\n<li>Outline of emergency notification procedures</li>\n<li>Description of how to determine the probable affected area and population by releases</li>\n<li>Description of local emergency equipment and facilities and the persons responsible for them</li>\n<li>Outline of evacuation plans</li>\n<li>A training program for emergency responders (including schedules)</li>\n<li>Methods and schedules for exercising emergency response plans</li>\n</ul>\n<p>According to the EPA, "Many LEPCs have expanded their activities beyond the requirements of EPCRA, encouraging accident prevention and risk reduction, and addressing homeland security in their communities" and the Agency offers advice on how to evaluate the effectiveness of these committees.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparedness_measures">Preparedness measures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Preparedness measures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px">\n<div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Camera-photo.svg" class="image" title="link={{{link}}}"><img alt="Small camera icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/40px-Camera-photo.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/60px-Camera-photo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/80px-Camera-photo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></a></div>\n</div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>The image captions</b> in this section <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup">require cleanup</a></b> to comply with <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Captions#Some_criteria_for_a_good_caption" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Captions">Wikipedia guidelines</a></b>&#160;for <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Captions#Wording" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Captions">trivial wording</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact"><span style="font-size:85%;"><br />\n<i>See <b>Wikipedia\'s <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Picture_tutorial" title="Wikipedia:Picture tutorial">picture tutorial</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Category:Wikipedia_image_help" title="Category:Wikipedia image help">image help pages</a></b> \xe2\x80\x93 review <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Image_use_policy" title="Wikipedia:Image use policy">policy on image use</a></b> and check the <b><a href="/wiki/Talk:Emergency_management" title="Talk:Emergency management">talk page</a></b> \xe2\x80\x93 visit the <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Graphics_Lab" title="Wikipedia:Graphics Lab">Graphics Lab</a></b> and <b><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a></b> if you can.</i></span> (June 2017)</span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Preparedness measures can take many forms ranging from focusing on individual people, locations or incidents to broader, government-based "all hazard" planning.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> There are a number of preparedness stages between "all hazard\' and individual planning, generally involving some combination of both mitigation and response planning. Business continuity planning encourages businesses to have a <a href="/wiki/Disaster_Recovery_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Disaster Recovery Plan">Disaster Recovery Plan</a>. Community- and faith-based organizations mitigation efforts promote field response teams and inter-agency planning.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Classroom_Response_Kit.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Classroom_Response_Kit.JPG/220px-Classroom_Response_Kit.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Classroom_Response_Kit.JPG/330px-Classroom_Response_Kit.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Classroom_Response_Kit.JPG/440px-Classroom_Response_Kit.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Classroom_Response_Kit.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nClassroom response kit</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>School-based response teams cover everything from live shooters to gas leaks and nearby bank robberies.&lt;refcite web|url=<a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://archive.ahrq.gov/prep/schoolprep/schoolprep.pdf">http://archive.ahrq.gov/prep/schoolprep/schoolprep.pdf</a> |format=PDF |title=School-Based Emergency preparedness&#160;: A National analysis and recommended Protocol |publisher=Archive.ahrq.gov |accessdate=2015-03-08}}&lt;/ref&gt; Educational institutions plan for cyberattacks and windstorms.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Industry specific guidance exists for horse farms,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> boat owners<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and more.</p>\n<p>Family preparedness for disaster is fairly unusual. A 2013 survey found that only 19% of American families felt that they were "very prepared" for a disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Still, there are many resources available for family disaster planning. The <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Homeland_Security" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a>\'s Ready.gov page includes a Family Emergency Plan Checklist,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> has a whole webpage devoted to readiness for kids, complete with cartoon-style superheroes,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and ran a Thunderclap Campaign in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Disease_Control" class="mw-redirect" title="Center for Disease Control">Center for Disease Control</a> has a Zombie Apocalypse website.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kitchen_Fire_Extinguisher.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Kitchen_Fire_Extinguisher.JPG/220px-Kitchen_Fire_Extinguisher.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Kitchen_Fire_Extinguisher.JPG/330px-Kitchen_Fire_Extinguisher.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Kitchen_Fire_Extinguisher.JPG/440px-Kitchen_Fire_Extinguisher.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kitchen_Fire_Extinguisher.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nKitchen fire extinguisher</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Disasters take a variety of forms to include <a href="/wiki/Earthquakes" class="mw-redirect" title="Earthquakes">earthquakes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tsunamis" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsunamis">tsunamis</a> or regular <a href="/wiki/Structure_fires" class="mw-redirect" title="Structure fires">structure fires</a>. That a disaster or emergency is not large scale in terms of population or acreage impacted or duration does not make it any less of a disaster for the people or area impacted and much can be learned about preparedness from so-called small disasters.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The Red Cross states that it responds to nearly 70,000 disasters a year, the most common of which is a single family fire.<sup id="cite_ref-akamai1_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akamai1-25">[25]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Items_on_Shelves_in_Basement.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Items_on_Shelves_in_Basement.JPG/220px-Items_on_Shelves_in_Basement.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Items_on_Shelves_in_Basement.JPG/330px-Items_on_Shelves_in_Basement.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Items_on_Shelves_in_Basement.JPG/440px-Items_on_Shelves_in_Basement.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Items_on_Shelves_in_Basement.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nItems on shelves in basement</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Preparedness starts with an individual\'s <a href="/wiki/Everyday_life" title="Everyday life">everyday life</a> and involves items and training that would be useful in an emergency. What is useful in an emergency is often also useful in everyday life.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> From personal preparedness, preparedness continues on a continuum through family preparedness, community preparedness and then business, non-profit and governmental preparedness. Some organizations blend these various levels. For example, the <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement</a> has a webpage on disaster training<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> as well as offering training on basic preparedness such as <a href="/wiki/Cardiopulmonary_resuscitation" title="Cardiopulmonary resuscitation">Cardiopulmonary resuscitation</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Aid" class="mw-redirect" title="First Aid">First Aid</a>. Other non-profits such as <a href="/wiki/Team_Rubicon" title="Team Rubicon">Team Rubicon</a> bring specific groups of people into disaster preparedness and response operations.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> FEMA breaks down preparedness into a pyramid, with citizens on the foundational bottom, on top of which rests local government, state government and federal government in that order.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Non_Perishable_Food_in_cabinet.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Non_Perishable_Food_in_cabinet.JPG/220px-Non_Perishable_Food_in_cabinet.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Non_Perishable_Food_in_cabinet.JPG/330px-Non_Perishable_Food_in_cabinet.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Non_Perishable_Food_in_cabinet.JPG/440px-Non_Perishable_Food_in_cabinet.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Non_Perishable_Food_in_cabinet.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nNon-perishable food in cabinet</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The basic theme behind preparedness is to be ready for an emergency and there are a number of different variations of being ready based on an assessment of what sort of threats exist. Nonetheless, there is basic guidance for preparedness that is common despite an area\'s specific dangers. FEMA recommends that everyone have a three-day survival kit for their household.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Because individual household sizes and specific needs might vary, FEMA\'s recommendations are not item specific, but the list includes:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Three-day supply of non-perishable food.</li>\n<li>Three-day supply of water \xe2\x80\x93 one gallon of water per person, per day.</li>\n<li>Portable, battery-powered radio or television and extra batteries.</li>\n<li>Flashlight and extra batteries.</li>\n<li>First aid kit and manual.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">Sanitation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hygiene" title="Hygiene">hygiene</a> items (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Toilet_paper" title="Toilet paper">toilet paper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feminine_hygiene" title="Feminine hygiene">menstrual hygiene products</a>).</li>\n<li>Matches and waterproof container.</li>\n<li>Whistle.</li>\n<li>Extra clothing.</li>\n<li>Kitchen accessories and cooking utensils, including a can opener.</li>\n<li>Photocopies of credit and identification cards.</li>\n<li>Cash and coins.</li>\n<li>Special needs items, such as prescription medications, eyeglasses, contact lens solutions, and hearing aid batteries.</li>\n<li>Items for infants, such as formula, diapers, bottles, and pacifiers.</li>\n<li>Other items to meet unique family needs.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Along similar lines, but not exactly the same, CDC has its own list for a proper disaster supply kit.<sup id="cite_ref-emergency.cdc.gov_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emergency.cdc.gov-31">[31]</a></sup></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Water\xe2\x80\x94one gallon per person, per day</li>\n<li>Food\xe2\x80\x94nonperishable, easy-to-prepare items</li>\n<li>Flashlight</li>\n<li>Battery powered or hand crank radio (NOAA Weather Radio, if possible)</li>\n<li>Extra batteries</li>\n<li>First aid kit</li>\n<li>Medications (7-day supply), other medical supplies, and medical paperwork (e.g., medication list and pertinent medical information)</li>\n<li>Multipurpose tool (e.g., Swiss army knife)</li>\n<li>Sanitation and personal hygiene items</li>\n<li>Copies of personal documents (e.g., proof of address, deed/lease to home, passports, birth certificates, and insurance policies)</li>\n<li>Cell phone with chargers</li>\n<li>Family and emergency contact information</li>\n<li>Extra cash</li>\n<li>Emergency blanket</li>\n<li>Map(s) of the area</li>\n<li>Extra set of car keys and house keys</li>\n<li>Manual can opener</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Children are a special population when considering Emergency preparedness and many resources are directly focused on supporting them. SAMHSA has list of tips for talking to children during infectious disease outbreaks, to include being a good listener, encouraging children to ask questions and modeling self-care by setting routines, eating healthy meals, getting enough sleep and taking deep breaths to handle stress.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> FEMA has similar advice, noting that "Disasters can leave children feeling frightened, confused, and insecure" whether a child has experienced it first hand, had it happen to a friend or simply saw it on television.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In the same publication, FEMA further notes, "Preparing for disaster helps everyone in the family accept the fact that disasters do happen, and provides an opportunity to identify and collect the resources needed to meet basic needs after disaster. Preparation helps; when people feel prepared, they cope better and so do children."</p>\n<p>To help people assess what threats might be in order to augment their emergency supplies or improve their disaster response skills, FEMA has published a booklet called the "Threat and Hazard Identification and Risk Assessment Guide."<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> (THIRA) This guide, which outlines the THIRA process, emphasizes "whole community involvement," not just governmental agencies, in preparedness efforts. In this guide, FEMA breaks down hazards into three categories: Natural, technological and human caused and notes that each hazard should be assessed for both its likelihood and its significance. According to FEMA, "Communities should consider only those threats and hazards that could plausibly occur" and "Communities should consider only those threats and hazards that would have a significant effect on them." To develop threat and hazard context descriptions, communities should take into account the time, place, and conditions in which threats or hazards might occur.</p>\n<p>Not all preparedness efforts and discussions involve the government or established NGOs like the Red Cross. Emergency preparation discussions are active on the internet, with many blogs and websites dedicated to discussing various aspects of preparedness. On-line sales of items such as survival food, medical supplies and heirloom seeds allow people to stock basements with cases of food and drinks with 25 year shelf lives, sophisticated medical kits and seeds that are guaranteed to sprout even after years of storage.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>One group of people who put a lot of effort in disaster preparations is called <a href="/wiki/Doomsday_Preppers" title="Doomsday Preppers">Doomsday Preppers</a>. This subset of preparedness-minded people often share a belief that the FEMA or Red Cross emergency preparation suggestions and training are not extensive enough. Sometimes called <a href="/wiki/Survivalists" class="mw-redirect" title="Survivalists">survivalists</a>, Doomsday Preppers are often preparing for The End Of The World As We Know It, abbreviated as TEOTWAWKI. With a motto some have that "The Future Belongs to those who Prepare," this Preparedness subset has its own set of Murphy\'s Rules,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> including "Rule Number 1: Food, you still don\'t have enough" and "Rule Number 26: People who thought the Government would save them, found out that it didn\'t."</p>\n<p>Not all emergency preparation efforts revolve around food, guns and shelters, though these items help address the needs in the bottom two sections of <a href="/wiki/Maslow%27s_hierarchy_of_needs" title="Maslow\'s hierarchy of needs">Maslow\'s hierarchy of needs</a>. The American Preppers Network<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> has an extensive list of items that might be useful in less apparent ways than a first aid kid or help add \'fun\' to challenging times. These items include:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Books and magazines</li>\n<li>Arts and crafts <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painting</a></li>\n<li>Children\'s entertainment</li>\n<li>Crayons and coloring books</li>\n<li>Notebooks and writing supplies</li>\n<li>Nuts, bolts, screws, nails, etc.</li>\n<li>Religious material</li>\n<li>Sporting equipment, card games and board games</li>\n<li>Posters and banners creating awareness</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Emergency preparedness goes beyond immediate family members. For many people, pets are an integral part of their families and emergency preparation advice includes them as well. It is not unknown for pet owners to die while trying to rescue their pets from a fire or from drowning.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> CDC\'s Disaster Supply Checklist for Pets includes:<sup id="cite_ref-emergency.cdc.gov_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emergency.cdc.gov-31">[31]</a></sup></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Food and water for at least 3 days for each pet; bowls, and a manual can opener.</li>\n<li>Depending on the pet you may need a litter box, paper towels, plastic trash bags, grooming items, and/or household bleach.</li>\n<li>Medications and medical records stored in a waterproof container.</li>\n<li>First aid kit with a pet first aid book.</li>\n<li>Sturdy leash, harness, and carrier to transport pet safely. A carrier should be large enough for the animal to stand comfortably, turn around, and lie down. Your pet may have to stay in the carrier for several hours.</li>\n<li>Pet toys and the pet\'s bed, if you can easily take it, to reduce stress.</li>\n<li>Current photos and descriptions of your pets to help others identify them in case you and your pets become separated, and to prove that they are yours.</li>\n<li>Information on feeding schedules, medical conditions, behavior problems, and the name and telephone number of your veterinarian in case you have to board your pets or place them in foster care.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Emergency preparedness also includes more than physical items and skill-specific training. Psychological preparedness is also a type of emergency preparedness and specific mental health preparedness resources are offered for mental health professionals by organizations such as the Red Cross.<sup id="cite_ref-akamai1_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akamai1-25">[25]</a></sup> These mental health preparedness resources are designed to support both community members affected by a disaster and the disaster workers serving them. CDC has a website devoted to coping with a disaster or traumatic event.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> After such an event, the CDC, through the <a href="/wiki/Substance_Abuse_and_Mental_Health_Services_Administration" title="Substance Abuse and Mental Health Services Administration">Substance Abuse and Mental Health Services Administration</a> (SAMHSA), suggests that people seek psychological help when they exhibit symptoms such as excessive worry, crying frequently, an increase in irritability, anger, and frequent arguing, wanting to be alone most of the time, feeling anxious or fearful, overwhelmed by sadness, confused, having trouble thinking clearly and concentrating, and difficulty making decisions, increased alcohol and/or substance use, increased physical (aches, pains) complaints such as headaches and trouble with "nerves."</p>\n<p>Sometimes emergency supplies are kept in what is called a <a href="/wiki/Bug-out_bag" title="Bug-out bag">Bug-out bag</a>. While FEMA does not actually use the term "Bug out bag," calling it instead some variation of a "Go Kit," the idea of having emergency items in a quickly accessible place is common to both FEMA and CDC, though on-line discussions of what items a "bug out bag" should include sometimes cover items such as firearms and great knives that are not specifically suggested by FEMA or CDC.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The theory behind a "bug out bag" is that emergency preparations should include the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Emergency_evacuation" title="Emergency evacuation">Emergency evacuation</a>. Whether fleeing a burning building or hastily packing a car to escape an impending hurricane, flood or dangerous chemical release, rapid departure from a home or workplace environment is always a possibility and FEMA suggests having a Family Emergency Plan for such occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-ready.gov_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ready.gov-41">[41]</a></sup> Because family members may not be together when disaster strikes, this plan should include reliable contact information for friends or relatives who live outside of what would be the disaster area for household members to notify they are safe or otherwise communicate with each other. Along with the contact information, FEMA suggests having well-understood local gathering points if a house must be evacuated quickly to avoid the dangers of re-reentering a burning home.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Family and emergency contact information should be printed on cards and put in each family member\'s backpack or wallet. If family members spend a significant amount of time in a specific location, such as at work or school, FEMA suggests learning the emergency preparation plans for those places.<sup id="cite_ref-ready.gov_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ready.gov-41">[41]</a></sup> FEMA has a specific form, in English and in Spanish, to help people put together these emergency plans, though it lacks lines for email contact information.<sup id="cite_ref-ready.gov_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ready.gov-41">[41]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Like children, people with disabilities and other special needs have special emergency preparation needs. While "disability" has a specific meaning for specific organizations such as collecting <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)" title="Social Security (United States)">Social Security</a> benefits,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> for the purposes of emergency preparedness, the Red Cross uses the term in a broader sense to include people with physical, medical, sensor or cognitive disabilities or the elderly and other special needs populations.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Depending on the particular disability, specific emergency preparations might be required. FEMA\'s suggestions for people with disabilities includes having copies of prescriptions, charging devices for medical devices such as motorized wheel chairs and a week\'s supply of medication readily available LINK or in a "go stay kit."<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> In some instances, lack of competency in English may lead to special preparation requirements and communication efforts for both individuals and responders.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>\n<p>FEMA notes that long term power outages can cause damage beyond the original disaster that can be mitigated with emergency generators or other power sources to provide an <a href="/wiki/Emergency_power_system" title="Emergency power system">Emergency power system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-47">[47]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">United States Department of Energy</a> states that \'homeowners, business owners, and local leaders may have to take an active role in dealing with energy disruptions on their own."<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> This active role may include installing or other procuring generators that are either portable or permanently mounted and run on fuels such as propane or natural gas<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> or gasoline.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Concerns about carbon monoxide poisoning, electrocution, flooding, fuel storage and fire lead even small property owners to consider professional installation and maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-47">[47]</a></sup> Major institutions like hospitals, military bases and educational institutions often have or are considering extensive backup power systems.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Instead of, or in addition to, fuel-based power systems, solar, wind and other alternative power sources may be used.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Standalone batteries, large or small, are also used to provide backup charging for electrical systems and devices ranging from emergency lights to computers to cell phones.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Emergency preparedness does not stop at home or at school.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Health_and_Human_Services" title="United States Department of Health and Human Services">United States Department of Health and Human Services</a> addresses specific emergency preparedness issues hospitals may have to respond to, including maintaining a safe temperature, providing adequate electricity for life support systems and even carrying out evacuations under extreme circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> FEMA encourages all businesses to have businesses to have an emergency response plan<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Small_Business_Administration" title="Small Business Administration">Small Business Administration</a> specifically advises small business owners to also focus emergency preparedness and provides a variety of different worksheets and resources.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>\n<p>FEMA cautions that emergencies happen while people are travelling as well<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and provides guidance around emergency preparedness for a range travelers to include commuters,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> <i>Commuter Emergency Plan</i> and holiday travelers.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> In particular, Ready.gov has a number of emergency preparations specifically designed for people with cars.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> These preparations include having a full gas tank, maintaining adequate windshield wiper fluid and other basic car maintenance tips. Items specific to an emergency include:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Jumper cables: might want to include flares or reflective triangle</li>\n<li>Flashlights, to include extra batteries (batteries have less power in colder weather)</li>\n<li>First Aid Kit, to include any necessary medications, baby formula and diapers if caring for small children</li>\n<li>Non-perishable food such as canned food (be alert to liquids freezing in colder weather), and protein rich foods like nuts and energy bars</li>\n<li>Manual can opener</li>\n<li>At least 1 gallon of water per person a day for at least 3 days (be alert to hazards of frozen water and resultant container rupture)</li>\n<li>Basic toolkit: pliers, wrench, screwdriver</li>\n<li>Pet supplies: food and water</li>\n<li>Radio: battery or hand cranked</li>\n<li>For snowy areas: cat litter or sand for better tire traction; shovel; ice scraper; warm clothes, gloves, hat, sturdy boots, jacket and an extra change of clothes</li>\n<li>Blankets or sleeping bags</li>\n<li>Charged Cell Phone: and car charger</li>\n</ul>\n<p>In addition to emergency supplies and training for various situations, FEMA offers advice on how to mitigate disasters. The Agency gives instructions on how to retrofit a home to minimize hazards from a <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">Flood</a>, to include installing a <a href="/wiki/Backflow_prevention_device" title="Backflow prevention device">Backflow prevention device</a>, anchoring fuel tanks and relocating electrical panels.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marked_gas_shuttoff.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Marked_gas_shuttoff.JPG/220px-Marked_gas_shuttoff.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Marked_gas_shuttoff.JPG/330px-Marked_gas_shuttoff.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Marked_gas_shuttoff.JPG/440px-Marked_gas_shuttoff.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marked_gas_shuttoff.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMarked gas shuttoff</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Given the explosive danger posed by <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> leaks, Ready.gov states unequivocally that "It is vital that all household members know how to shut off natural gas" and that property owners must ensure they have any special tools needed for their particular gas hookups. Ready.gov also notes that "It is wise to teach all responsible household members where and how to shut off the electricity," cautioning that individual circuits should be shut off before the main circuit. Ready.gov further states that "It is vital that all household members learn how to shut off the water at the main house valve" and cautions that the possibility that rusty valves might require replacement.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Response">Response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Disaster_response" title="Disaster response">Disaster response</a></div>\n<p>The response phase of an emergency may commence with <a href="/wiki/Search_and_Rescue" class="mw-redirect" title="Search and Rescue">Search and Rescue</a> but in all cases the focus will quickly turn to fulfilling the basic <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Humanitarian">humanitarian</a> <a href="/wiki/Basic_needs" title="Basic needs">needs</a> of the affected population. This assistance may be provided by national or international agencies and organizations. Effective coordination of disaster assistance is often crucial, particularly when many organizations respond and local emergency management agency (LEMA) capacity has been exceeded by the demand or diminished by the disaster itself. The <a href="/wiki/National_Response_Framework" title="National Response Framework">National Response Framework</a> is a United States government publication that explains responsibilities and expectations of government officials at the local, state, federal, and tribal levels. It provides guidance on Emergency Support Functions that may be integrated in whole or parts to aid in the response and recovery process.</p>\n<p>On a personal level the response can take the shape either of a <i><a href="/wiki/Shelter_in_place" title="Shelter in place">shelter in place</a></i> or an <i><a href="/wiki/Emergency_evacuation" title="Emergency evacuation">evacuation</a></i>.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Evacuation_sign.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Evacuation_sign.jpg/220px-Evacuation_sign.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Evacuation_sign.jpg/330px-Evacuation_sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Evacuation_sign.jpg/440px-Evacuation_sign.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Evacuation_sign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nEvacuation sign</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In a shelter-in-place scenario, a family would be prepared to fend for themselves in their home for many days without any form of outside support. In an <i>evacuation</i>, a family leaves the area by <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automobile</a> or other mode of <a href="/wiki/Transportation" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation">transportation</a>, taking with them the maximum amount of supplies they can carry, possibly including a tent for shelter. If mechanical transportation is not available, evacuation on foot would ideally include carrying at least three days of supplies and rain-tight bedding, a <a href="/wiki/Tarpaulin" title="Tarpaulin">tarpaulin</a> and a bedroll of blankets.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Donation" title="Donation">Donations</a> are often sought during this period, especially for large disasters that overwhelm local capacity. Due to efficiencies of scale, <a href="/wiki/Money" title="Money">money</a> is often the most cost-effective donation if fraud is avoided. Money is also the most flexible, and if goods are sourced locally then transportation is minimized and the local economy is boosted. Some donors prefer to send <a href="/wiki/Gifts_in_kind" title="Gifts in kind">gifts in kind</a>, however these items can end up creating issues, rather than helping. One innovation by <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Sandy" title="Occupy Sandy">Occupy Sandy</a> volunteers is to use a donation registry, where families and businesses impacted by the disaster can make specific requests, which remote donors can purchase directly via a web site.</p>\n<p>Medical considerations will vary greatly based on the type of disaster and secondary effects. Survivors may sustain a multitude of injuries to include <a href="/wiki/Lacerations" class="mw-redirect" title="Lacerations">lacerations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burn" title="Burn">burns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Near_drowning" class="mw-redirect" title="Near drowning">near drowning</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Crush_syndrome" title="Crush syndrome">crush syndrome</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recovery">Recovery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Recovery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The recovery phase starts after the immediate threat to human life has subsided. The immediate goal of the recovery phase is to bring the affected area back to normalcy as quickly as possible. During reconstruction it is recommended to consider the location or construction material of the property.</p>\n<p>The most extreme home confinement scenarios include war, <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a> and severe <a href="/wiki/Epidemic" title="Epidemic">epidemics</a> and may last a year or more. Then recovery will take place inside the home. Planners for these events usually buy <a href="/wiki/Bulk_purchasing" title="Bulk purchasing">bulk</a> foods and appropriate storage and preparation equipment, and eat the food as part of normal life. A simple balanced diet can be constructed from <a href="/wiki/Vitamin" title="Vitamin">vitamin</a> pills, <a href="/wiki/Whole-meal" class="mw-redirect" title="Whole-meal">whole-meal</a> wheat, beans, <a href="/wiki/Dried_milk" class="mw-redirect" title="Dried milk">dried milk</a>, corn, and <a href="/wiki/Cooking_oil" title="Cooking oil">cooking oil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Vegetables, fruits, spices and meats, both prepared and fresh-gardened, are included when possible.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="As_a_profession">As a profession</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: As a profession">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(March 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Professional emergency managers can focus on government and community preparedness, or private business preparedness. Training is provided by local, state, federal and private organizations and ranges from public information and media relations to high-level incident command and tactical skills.</p>\n<p>In the past, the field of emergency management has been populated mostly by people with a military or first responder background. Currently, the field has become more diverse, with many managers coming from a variety of backgrounds other than the military or first responder fields. Educational opportunities are increasing for those seeking undergraduate and graduate degrees in emergency management or a related field. There are over 180 schools in the US with emergency management-related programs, but only one doctoral program specifically in emergency management.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Professional certifications such as Certified Emergency Manager (CEM)<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> and Certified Business Continuity Professional (CBCP) are becoming more common as professional standards are raised throughout the field, particularly in the United States. There are also professional organizations for emergency managers, such as the National Emergency Management Association and the International Association of Emergency Managers.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Principles">Principles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Principles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2007, Dr. Wayne Blanchard of FEMA\'s Emergency Management Higher Education Project, at the direction of Dr. Cortez Lawrence, Superintendent of FEMA\'s Emergency Management Institute, convened a working group of emergency management practitioners and academics to consider principles of emergency management. This was the first time the principles of the discipline were to be codified. The group agreed on eight principles that will be used to guide the development of a doctrine of emergency management. Below is a summary:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>Comprehensive \xe2\x80\x93 consider and take into account all hazards, all phases, all stakeholders and all impacts relevant to disasters.</li>\n<li>Progressive \xe2\x80\x93 anticipate future disasters and take preventive and preparatory measures to build disaster-resistant and disaster-resilient communities.</li>\n<li>Risk-driven \xe2\x80\x93 use sound risk management principles (hazard identification, risk analysis, and impact analysis) in assigning priorities and resources.</li>\n<li>Integrated \xe2\x80\x93 ensure <a href="/wiki/Unity_of_effort" title="Unity of effort">unity of effort</a> among all levels of government and all elements of a community.</li>\n<li>Collaborative \xe2\x80\x93 create and sustain broad and sincere relationships among individuals and organizations to encourage trust, advocate a team atmosphere, build consensus, and facilitate communication.</li>\n<li>Coordinated \xe2\x80\x93 synchronize the activities of all relevant stakeholders to achieve a common purpose.</li>\n<li>Flexible \xe2\x80\x93 use creative and innovative approaches in solving disaster challenges.</li>\n<li>Professional \xe2\x80\x93 value a science and knowledge-based approach; based on education, training, experience, ethical practice, public stewardship and continuous improvement.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>A fuller description of these principles can be found at<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tools">Tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In recent years the continuity feature of emergency management has resulted in a new concept, <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Management_Information_System" title="Emergency Management Information System">Emergency Management Information Systems</a> (EMIS). For continuity and inter-operability between emergency management stakeholders, EMIS supports an infrastructure that integrates emergency plans at all levels of government and non-government involvement for all four phases of emergencies. In the healthcare field, hospitals utilize the <a href="/wiki/Hospital_Incident_Command_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Hospital Incident Command System">Hospital Incident Command System</a> (HICS), which provides structure and organization in a clearly defined chain of command.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disaster_response_technologies">Disaster response technologies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Disaster response technologies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Smart Emergency Response System (SERS)<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> prototype was built in the SmartAmerica Challenge 2013-2014, a United States government initiative. SERS has been created by a team of nine organizations led by MathWorks. The project was featured at the White House in June 2014 and described by Todd Park (U.S. Chief Technology Officer) as an exemplary achievement.</p>\n<p>The Smart America initiative challenges the participants to build cyber-physical systems as a glimpse of the future to save lives, create jobs, foster businesses, and improve the economy. SERS primarily saves lives. The system provides the survivors and the emergency personnel with information to locate and assist each other during a disaster. SERS allows to submit help requests to a MATLAB-based mission center connecting first responders, apps, search-and-rescue dogs, a 6-feet-tall humanoid, robots, drones, and autonomous aircraft and ground vehicles. The command and control center optimizes the available resources to serve every incoming requests and generates an action plan for the mission. The Wi-Fi network is created on the fly by the drones equipped with antennas. In addition, the autonomous rotorcrafts, planes, and ground vehicles are simulated with Simulink and visualized in a 3D environment (Google Earth) to unlock the ability to observe the operations on a mass scale.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Within_other_professions">Within other professions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Within other professions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(March 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rockefeller_University_Disaster_Plan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Rockefeller_University_Disaster_Plan.jpg/220px-Rockefeller_University_Disaster_Plan.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Rockefeller_University_Disaster_Plan.jpg/330px-Rockefeller_University_Disaster_Plan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Rockefeller_University_Disaster_Plan.jpg/440px-Rockefeller_University_Disaster_Plan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rockefeller_University_Disaster_Plan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA disaster plan book at <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_University" title="Rockefeller University">Rockefeller University</a> in a biochemistry research laboratory.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Practitioners in emergency management come from an increasing variety of backgrounds. Professionals from <a href="/wiki/Memory_institution" title="Memory institution">memory institutions</a> (e.g., museums, historical societies, etc.) are dedicated to preserving cultural heritage\xe2\x80\x94objects and records. This has been an increasingly major component within this field as a result of the heightened awareness following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> in 2001, the <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">hurricanes in 2005</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Historical_Archive_of_the_City_of_Cologne" title="Historical Archive of the City of Cologne">collapse of the Cologne Archives</a>.</p>\n<p>To increase the potential successful recovery of valuable records, a well-established and thoroughly tested plan must be developed. This plan should emphasize simplicity in order to aid in response and recovery: employees should perform similar tasks in the response and recovery phase that they perform under normal conditions. It should also include mitigation strategies such as the installation of sprinklers within the institution.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Professional associations hold regular workshops to keep individuals up to date with tools and resources in order to minimize risk and maximize recovery.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_tools">Other tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Other tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Agency_for_International_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Agency for International Development">U.S. Agency for International Development</a> created a web-based tool for estimating populations impacted by disasters. Called Population Explorer<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> the tool uses land scan population data, developed by <a href="/wiki/Oak_Ridge_National_Laboratory" title="Oak Ridge National Laboratory">Oak Ridge National Laboratory</a>, to distribute population at a resolution 1&#160;km<sup>2</sup> for all countries in the world. Used by USAID\'s <a href="/wiki/Famine_Early_Warning_System_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Famine Early Warning System Network">FEWS NET</a> Project to estimate populations vulnerable and or imd by food insecurity, Population Explorer is gaining wide use in a range of emergency analysis and response actions, including estimating populations impacted by floods in Central America and the Pacific Ocean tsunami event in 2009.</p>\n<p>In 2007, a checklist for veterinarians was published in the Journal of the American Veterinary Medical Association, it had two sets of questions for a professional to ask themselves before assisting with an emergency:</p>\n<p><b>Absolute requirements for participation:</b></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Have I chosen to participate?</li>\n<li>Have I taken ICS training?</li>\n<li>Have I taken other required background courses?</li>\n<li>Have I made arrangements with my practice to deploy?</li>\n<li>Have I made arrangements with my family?</li>\n</ul>\n<p><b>Incident Participation:</b></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Have I been invited to participate?</li>\n<li>Are my skill sets a match for the mission?</li>\n<li>Can I access just-in-time training to refresh skills or acquire needed new skills?</li>\n<li>Is this a self-support mission?</li>\n<li>Do I have supplies needed for three to five days of self-support?</li>\n</ul>\n<p>While written for veterinarians, this checklist is applicable for any professional to consider before assisting with an emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_organizations">International organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: International organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_International_Emergency_Management_Society">The International Emergency Management Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: The International Emergency
