Management Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_International_Emergency_Management_Society&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The International Emergency Management Society (page does not exist)">The International Emergency Management Society</a> (TIEMS), is an international non-profit NGO, registered in Belgium. TIEMS is a Global Forum for Education, Training, Certification and Policy in Emergency and Disaster Management. TIEMS\' goal is to develop and bring modern emergency management tools, and techniques into practice, through the exchange of information, methodology innovations and new technologies.</p>\n<p>TIEMS provides a platform for stakeholders to meet, network and learn about new technical and operational methodologies. TIEMS focuses on cultural differences to be understood and included in the society\'s events, education and research programs. This is achieved by establishing local chapters worldwide. Today, TIEMS has chapters in Benelux, Romania, Finland, Italy, Middle East and North Africa (MENA), Iraq, India, Korea, Japan and China.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Association_of_Emergency_Managers">International Association of Emergency Managers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: International Association of Emergency Managers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Emergency_Managers" title="International Association of Emergency Managers">International Association of Emergency Managers</a> (IAEM) is a non-profit educational organization aimed at promoting the goals of saving lives and property protection during emergencies. The mission of IAEM is to serve its members by providing information, networking and professional opportunities, and to advance the emergency management profession.</p>\n<p>It has seven councils around the world: Asia,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Europa,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> International,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Oceania,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Student<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> and USA.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Air Force Emergency Management Association, affiliated by membership with the IAEM, provides emergency management information and networking for <a href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force_Emergency_Management" title="U.S. Air Force Emergency Management">U.S. Air Force Emergency Management</a> personnel.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Recovery_Platform">International Recovery Platform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: International Recovery Platform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The International Recovery Platform (IRP) was conceived at the World Conference on Disaster Reduction (WCDR) in Kobe, Hyogo, Japan in January 2005, as part of the <i>Hyogo Framework for Action (HFA) 2005\xe2\x80\x932015</i>. The HFA is a global plan for disaster risk reduction adopted by 168 governments.</p>\n<p>The key role of IRP is to identify gaps in post disaster recovery and to serve as a catalyst for the development of tools and resources for recovery efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement">The International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: The International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Societies" title="International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies">International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies</a> (IFRC) works closely with National Red Cross and Red Crescent societies in responding to emergencies, many times playing a pivotal role. In addition, the IFRC may deploy assessment teams, e.g. Field Assessment and Coordination Teams (FACT),<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> to the affected country if requested by the national society. After assessing the needs, <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Response_Unit" title="Emergency Response Unit">Emergency Response Units</a> (ERUs)<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> may be deployed to the affected country or region. They are specialized in the response component of the emergency management framework.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baptist_Global_Response">Baptist Global Response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Baptist Global Response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Baptist Global Response (BGR) is a disaster relief and community development organization. BGR and its partners respond globally to people with critical needs worldwide, whether those needs arise from chronic conditions or acute crises such as natural disasters. While BGR is not an official entity of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>, it is rooted in Southern Baptist life and is the international partnership of Southern Baptist Disaster Relief teams, which operate primarily in the US and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations">United Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: United Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> system rests with the Resident Coordinator within the affected country. However, in practice, the UN response will be coordinated by the UN <a href="/wiki/Office_for_the_Coordination_of_Humanitarian_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs">Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs</a> (UN-OCHA), by deploying a <a href="/wiki/UN_Disaster_Assessment_and_Coordination" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Disaster Assessment and Coordination">UN Disaster Assessment and Coordination</a> (UNDAC) team, in response to a request by the affected country\'s government. Finally <a href="/wiki/UN-SPIDER" title="UN-SPIDER">UN-SPIDER</a> designed as a networking hub to support disaster management by application of satellite technology<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Bank">World Bank</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: World Bank">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since 1980, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> has approved more than 500 projects related to disaster management, dealing with both disaster mitigation as well as reconstruction projects, amounting to more than US$40 billion. These projects have taken place all over the world, in countries such as Argentina, Bangladesh, Colombia, Haiti, India, Mexico, Turkey and Vietnam.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank1_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank1-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-worldbank1_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank1-85">[85]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Prevention and mitigation projects include forest fire prevention measures, such as early warning measures and education campaigns; early-warning systems for hurricanes; flood prevention mechanisms (e.g. shore protection, terracing, etc.); and earthquake-prone construction.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank1_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank1-85">[85]</a></sup> In a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> under the umbrella of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=ProVention_Consortium&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ProVention Consortium (page does not exist)">ProVention Consortium</a> the World Bank has established a Global Risk Analysis of Natural Disaster Hotspots.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In June 2006, the World Bank, in response to the HFA, established the Global Facility for Disaster Reduction and Recovery (GFDRR), a partnership with other aid donors to reduce disaster losses. GFDRR helps developing countries fund development projects and programs that enhance local capacities for disaster prevention and emergency preparedness.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2001 the EU adopted Community Mechanism for Civil Protection, to facilitate co-operation in the event of major emergencies requiring urgent response actions. This also applies to situations where there may be an imminent threat as well.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The heart of the Mechanism is the Monitoring and Information Center (MIC), part of the European Commission\'s Directorate-General for Humanitarian Aid &amp; Civil Protection. Accessible 24 hours a day, it gives countries access to a one-stop-shop of civil protections available amongst all the participating states. Any country inside or outside the Union affected by a major disaster can make an appeal for assistance through the MIC. It acts as a communication hub, and provides useful and updated information on the actual status of an ongoing emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_organizations">National organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: National organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(March 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Management_in_Australia" title="Emergency Management in Australia">Emergency Management in Australia</a></div>\n<p>Naers are part of life in Australia. Heatwaves have killed more Australians than any other type of natural disaster in the 20th century. Australia\'s emergency management processes embrace the concept of the prepared community. The principal government agency in achieving this is <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Management_Australia" title="Emergency Management Australia">Emergency Management Australia</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Public_Safety_Canada" title="Public Safety Canada">Public Safety Canada</a> is Canada\'s national emergency management agency. Each province is required to have both legislation for dealing with emergencies, and provincial emergency management agencies, typically called "Emergency Measures Organizations" (EMO). Public Safety Canada co-ordinates and supports the efforts of federal organizations as well as other levels of government, first responders, community groups, the private sector, and other nations. The Public Safety and Emergency Preparedness Act defines the powers, duties and functions of PS are outlined. Other acts are specific to individual fields such as corrections, law enforcement, and national security.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> the Federal Government controls the German <i>Katastrophenschutz</i> (disaster relief), the <a href="/wiki/Technisches_Hilfswerk" title="Technisches Hilfswerk">Technisches Hilfswerk</a> (<i>Federal Agency for Technical Relief</i>, THW), and the <i>Zivilschutz</i> (<a href="/wiki/Civil_defense" title="Civil defense">civil protection</a>) programs coordinated by the <i>Federal Office of Civil Protection and Disaster Assistance</i>. Local <a href="/wiki/German_fire_department" class="mw-redirect" title="German fire department">fire department</a> units, the German Armed Forces (<a href="/wiki/Bundeswehr" title="Bundeswehr">Bundeswehr</a>), the <a href="/wiki/German_Federal_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="German Federal Police">German Federal Police</a> and the 16 state police forces (L\xc3\xa4nderpolizei) are also deployed during disaster relief operations.</p>\n<p>There are several private organizations in Germany that also deal with emergency relief. Among these are the German Red Cross, <a href="/wiki/Johanniter-Unfall-Hilfe" title="Johanniter-Unfall-Hilfe">Johanniter-Unfall-Hilfe</a> (the German equivalent of the St. John Ambulance), the Malteser-Hilfsdienst, and the <a href="/wiki/Arbeiter-Samariter-Bund_Deutschland" title="Arbeiter-Samariter-Bund Deutschland">Arbeiter-Samariter-Bund</a>. As of 2006, there is a program of study at the University of Bonn leading to the degree "Master in Disaster Prevention and Risk Governance"<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> As a support function <a href="/wiki/Radio_amateurs" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio amateurs">radio amateurs</a> provide additional emergency communication networks with frequent trainings.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wall_in_kalpakkam.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Wall_in_kalpakkam.JPG/200px-Wall_in_kalpakkam.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Wall_in_kalpakkam.JPG/300px-Wall_in_kalpakkam.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Wall_in_kalpakkam.JPG/400px-Wall_in_kalpakkam.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wall_in_kalpakkam.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA protective wall built on the shore of the coastal town of <a href="/wiki/Kalpakkam" title="Kalpakkam">Kalpakkam</a>, in aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">2004 Indian Ocean earthquake</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Disaster_Management_Authority_(India)" title="National Disaster Management Authority (India)">National Disaster Management Authority</a> is the primary government agency responsible for planning and capacity-building for disaster relief. Its emphasis is primarily on strategic risk management and mitigation, as well as developing policies and planning.<sup id="cite_ref-ndma-functions_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ndma-functions-91">[91]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Disaster_Management" title="National Institute of Disaster Management">National Institute of Disaster Management</a> is a policy think-tank and training institution for developing guidelines and training programs for mitigating disasters and managing crisis response.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Disaster_Response_Force" title="National Disaster Response Force">National Disaster Response Force</a> is the government agency primarily responsible for emergency management during <a href="/wiki/Natural_disaster" title="Natural disaster">natural</a> and <a href="/wiki/Man-made_disasters" class="mw-redirect" title="Man-made disasters">man-made disasters</a>, with specialized skills in search, rescue and rehabilitation.<sup id="cite_ref-about_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-92">[92]</a></sup> The Ministry of Science and Technology also contains an agency that brings the expertise of earth scientists and meteorologists to emergency management. The <a href="/wiki/Indian_Armed_Forces" title="Indian Armed Forces">Indian Armed Forces</a> also plays an important role in the rescue/recovery operations after disasters.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Aniruddha%27s_Academy_of_Disaster_Management" title="Aniruddha\'s Academy of Disaster Management">Aniruddha\'s Academy of Disaster Management</a> (AADM) is a non-profit organization in Mumbai, India with \'disaster management\' as its principal objective.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, The National Security Council has the responsibility to handle emergency and disaster events. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ministry_of_Home_Affairs_Malaysia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ministry of Home Affairs Malaysia (page does not exist)">Ministry of Home Affairs Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_Malaysia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Health Malaysia">Ministry of Health Malaysia</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ministry_of_Housing,_Urban_Wellbeing_and_Local_Government_Malaysia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ministry of Housing, Urban Wellbeing and Local Government Malaysia (page does not exist)">Ministry of Housing, Urban Wellbeing and Local Government Malaysia</a> are also having responsibility in managing emergency. Several agencies are involved in emergency managements are <a href="/wiki/Royal_Malaysian_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Malaysian Police">Royal Malaysian Police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_Fire_and_Rescue_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Malaysian Fire and Rescue Department">Malaysian Fire and Rescue Department</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_Civil_Defence_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Malaysian Civil Defence Force">Malaysian Civil Defence Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_Malaysia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Health Malaysia">Ministry of Health Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_Maritime_Enforcement_Agency" title="Malaysian Maritime Enforcement Agency">Malaysian Maritime Enforcement Agency</a>. There were also some voluntary organisation who involved themselves in emergency/ disaster management such as <a href="/wiki/St._John_Ambulance_of_Malaysia" title="St. John Ambulance of Malaysia">St. John Ambulance of Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_Red_Crescent_Society" title="Malaysian Red Crescent Society">Malaysian Red Crescent Society</a> and so on.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nepal">Nepal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Nepal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Nepal Risk Reduction Consortium (NRRC) is based on hyogo Framework and Nepal\'s National Strategy for Disaster Risk Management. This arrangement unites humanitarian and development partners with Government of Nepal and had identified 5 flagship priorities for sustainable disaster risk management.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, depending on the scope of the emergency/disaster, responsibility may be handled at either the local or national level. Within each region, local governments are organized into 16 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Civil_Defence_Emergency_Management_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Civil Defence Emergency Management Group (page does not exist)">Civil Defence Emergency Management Groups</a> (CMGs). If local arrangements are overwhelmed, pre-existing mutual-support arrangements are activated. Central government has the authority to coordinate the response through the <a href="/wiki/National_Crisis_Management_Centre" title="National Crisis Management Centre">National Crisis Management Centre</a> (NCMC), operated by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Civil_Defence_%26_Emergency_Management_(New_Zealand)" title="Ministry of Civil Defence &amp; Emergency Management (New Zealand)">Ministry of Civil Defence &amp; Emergency Management</a> (MCDEM). These structures are defined by regulation,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> and explained in <i>The Guide to the National Civil Defence Emergency Management Plan 2006</i>, roughly equivalent to the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/National_Response_Framework" title="National Response Framework">National Response Framework</a>.</p>\n<p>New Zealand uses unique terminology for emergency management. Emergency management is rarely used, many government publications retaining the use of the term civil defence.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> For example, the Minister of Civil Defence is responsible for the MCDEM. Civil Defence Emergency Management is a term in its own right, defined by statute.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> And disaster rarely appears in official publications, emergency and incident being the preferred terms,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> with the term event also being used. For example, publications refer to the <a href="/wiki/Canterbury_(New_Zealand)" class="mw-redirect" title="Canterbury (New Zealand)">Canterbury</a> Snow Event 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>\n<p>"4Rs" is the emergency management cycle used in New Zealand, its four phases are known as:<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Reduction = Mitigation</li>\n<li>Readiness = Preparedness</li>\n<li>Response</li>\n<li>Recovery</li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Disaster management in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> revolves around flood disasters focusing on rescue and relief.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Federal_Flood_Commission" title="Federal Flood Commission">Federal Flood Commission</a> was established in 1977 under <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Water_and_Power_(Pakistan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Water and Power (Pakistan)">Ministry of Water and Power</a> to manage the issues of flood management on country-wide basis.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=National_Disaster_Management_Ordinance,_2006&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="National Disaster Management Ordinance, 2006 (page does not exist)">National Disaster Management Ordinance, 2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Disaster_Management_Act,_2010" title="National Disaster Management Act, 2010">National Disaster Management Act, 2010</a> were enacted after <a href="/wiki/2005_Kashmir_earthquake" title="2005 Kashmir earthquake">2005 Kashmir earthquake</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_Pakistan_floods" title="2010 Pakistan floods">2010 Pakistan floods</a> respectively to deal with disaster management. The primary central authority mandated to deal with whole spectrum of disasters and their management in the country is <a href="/wiki/National_Disaster_Management_Authority_(Pakistan)" title="National Disaster Management Authority (Pakistan)">National Disaster Management Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In addition each <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Pakistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Province of Pakistan">province</a> along with <a href="/wiki/FATA_Disaster_Management_Authority" title="FATA Disaster Management Authority">FATA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilgit_Baltistan_Disaster_Management_Authority" title="Gilgit Baltistan Disaster Management Authority">Gilgit Baltistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/State_Disaster_Management_Authority_(Azad_Jammu_%26_Kashmir)" title="State Disaster Management Authority (Azad Jammu &amp; Kashmir)">Pakistani administered Kashmir</a> has its own provincial disaster management authority responsible for implementing policies and plans for Disaster Management in the Province.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Each <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Pakistan" title="Districts of Pakistan">District</a> has its own District Disaster Management Authority for planning, coordinating and implementing body for disaster management and take all measures for the purposes of disaster management in the districts in accordance with the guidelines laid down by the National Authority and the Provincial Authority.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Disaster_Risk_Reduction_and_Management_Council" title="National Disaster Risk Reduction and Management Council">National Disaster Risk Reduction and Management Council</a> is responsible for the protection and welfare of people during disasters or emergencies. It is a working group composed of various government, non-government, civil sector and private sector organizations of the Government of the Republic of the Philippines. Headed by the Secretary of National Defense (under the Office of Civil Defense, the NDRRMCs implementing organization), it coordinates all the executive branches of government, presidents of the leagues of local government units throughout the country, the <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Philippines" title="Armed Forces of the Philippines">Armed Forces of the Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippine_National_Police" title="Philippine National Police">Philippine National Police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Fire_Protection" title="Bureau of Fire Protection">Bureau of Fire Protection</a> (which is an agency under the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Interior_and_Local_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Interior and Local Government">Department of Interior and Local Government</a>, and the public and private medical services in responding to natural and manmade disasters, as well as planning, coordination, and training of these responsible units. Non-governmental organizations such as the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Red_Cross" title="Philippine Red Cross">Philippine Red Cross</a> also provide manpower and material support for NDRRMC.</p>\n<p>Regional, provincial, city, municipal, and barangay emergency management are handled by Local Disaster Risk Reduction Management Councils (LDRRMCs), which are the functional arm of the local government unit (LGU). Each LDRRMC is headed by a Chief DRRM Officer, and each Office is tasked to organize their own emergency teams and command-and-control centers when activated at times of local emergencies (identified on the regional, provincial, city, municipal, and/or barangay level).</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Emergency_Situations_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Emergency Situations (Russia)">Ministry of Emergency Situations</a> (EMERCOM) is engaged in <a href="/wiki/Fire_fighting" class="mw-redirect" title="Fire fighting">fire fighting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Civil_defense" title="Civil defense">civil defense</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Search_and_rescue" title="Search and rescue">search and rescue</a> after both natural and human-made disasters.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Somalia">Somalia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Somalia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Government_of_Somalia" title="Federal Government of Somalia">Federal Government</a> announced in May 2013 that the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Council_of_Ministers" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali Council of Ministers">Cabinet</a> had approved draft legislation on a new <a href="/wiki/Somali_Disaster_Management_Agency" title="Somali Disaster Management Agency">Somali Disaster Management Agency</a> (SDMA), which had originally been proposed by the Ministry of Interior. According to the Prime Minister\'s Media Office, the SDMA will lead and coordinate the government\'s response to various natural disasters. It is part of a broader effort by the federal authorities to re-establish national institutions. The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Parliament_of_Somalia" title="Federal Parliament of Somalia">Federal Parliament</a> is now expected to deliberate on the proposed bill for endorsement after any amendments.<sup id="cite_ref-Rsp_Mcfp_Tel_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rsp_Mcfp_Tel-106">[106]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Netherlands">The Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: The Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Security_and_Justice_(Netherlands)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Security and Justice (Netherlands)">Ministry of Security and Justice</a> is responsible for emergency preparedness and emergency management on a national level and operates a national crisis centre (NCC). The country is divided into 25 safety regions (<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/veiligheidsregio" class="extiw" title="nl:veiligheidsregio">veiligheidsregio</a>). In a safety region, there are four components: the regional fire department, the regional department for medical care(ambulances and psycho-sociological care etc.), the regional dispatch and a section for risk- and crisis management. The regional dispatch operates for police, fire department and the regional medical care. The dispatch has all these three services combined into one dispatch for the best multi-coordinated response to an incident or an emergency. And also facilitates in information management, emergency communication and care of citizens. These services are the main structure for a response to an emergency. It can happen that, for a specific emergency, the co-operation with an other service is needed, for instance the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Netherlands)" title="Ministry of Defence (Netherlands)">Ministry of Defence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_board" title="Water board">water board</a>(s) or <a href="/wiki/Rijkswaterstaat" title="Rijkswaterstaat">Rijkswaterstaat</a>. The veiligheidsregio can integrate these other services into their structure by adding them to specific conferences on operational or administrative level.</p>\n<p>All regions operate according to the <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Regional_Incident_Management_(Netherlands)" title="Coordinated Regional Incident Management (Netherlands)">Coordinated Regional Incident Management</a> system.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Following the 2000 <a href="/wiki/UK_fuel_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="UK fuel protests">fuel protests</a> and severe flooding that same year, as well as the <a href="/wiki/2001_United_Kingdom_foot-and-mouth_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2001 United Kingdom foot-and-mouth crisis">foot-and-mouth</a> crisis in 2001, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> passed the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Contingencies_Act_2004" title="Civil Contingencies Act 2004">Civil Contingencies Act 2004</a> (CCA). The CCA defined some organisations as Category 1 and 2 Responders, setting responsibilities regarding emergency preparedness and response. It is managed by the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Contingencies_Secretariat" title="Civil Contingencies Secretariat">Civil Contingencies Secretariat</a> through Regional Resilience Forums and local authorities.</p>\n<p>Disaster Management training is generally conducted at the local level, and consolidated through professional courses that can be taken at the <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Planning_College" title="Emergency Planning College">Emergency Planning College</a>. Diplomas, undergraduate and postgraduate qualifications can be gained at universities throughout the country. The Institute of Emergency Management is a charity, established in 1996, providing consulting services for the government, media and commercial sectors. There are a number of professional societies for Emergency Planners including the Emergency Planning Society<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> and the Institute of Civil Protection and Emergency Management.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>\n<p>One of the largest emergency exercises in the UK was carried out on 20 May 2007 near <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>: a simulated plane crash-landing at <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International_Airport" title="Belfast International Airport">Belfast International Airport</a>. Staff from five hospitals and three airports participated in the drill, and almost 150 international observers assessed its effectiveness.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Disaster management in the United States has utilized the functional All-Hazards approach for over 20 years, in which managers develop processes (such as communication &amp; warning or sheltering) rather than developing single-hazard or threat focused plans (e.g., a tornado plan). Processes are then mapped to specific hazards or threats, with the manager looking for gaps, overlaps, and conflicts between processes.</p>\n<p>Given these notions, emergency managers must identify, contemplate, and assess possible man-made threats and natural threats that may affect their respective locales.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Because of geographical differences throughout the nation, a variety of different threats affect communities among the states. Thus, although similarities may exist, no two emergency plans will be completely identical. Additionally, each locale has different resources and capacities (e.g., budgets, personnel, equipment, etc.) for dealing with emergencies.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Each individual community must craft its own unique emergency plan that addresses potential threats that are specific to the locality.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>\n<p>This creates a plan more resilient to unique events because all common processes are defined, and it encourages planning done by the stakeholders who are closer to the individual processes, such as a traffic management plan written by a public works director. This type of planning can lead to conflict with non-emergency management regulatory bodies, which require the development of hazard/threat specific plans, such as the development of specific H1N1 flu plans and terrorism-specific plans.</p>\n<p>In the United States, all disasters are initially local, with local authorities, with usually a police, fire, or EMS agency, taking charge. Many local municipalities may also have a separate dedicated <a href="/wiki/Office_of_emergency_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of emergency management">office of emergency management</a> (OEM), along with personnel and equipment. If the event becomes overwhelming to the local government, state emergency management (the primary government structure of the United States) becomes the controlling emergency management agency. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency of the United States">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA), part of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a> (DHS), is the lead federal agency for emergency management. The United States and its territories are broken down into ten regions for FEMA\'s emergency management purposes. FEMA supports, but does not override, state authority.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Citizen_Corps" title="Citizen Corps">Citizen Corps</a> is an organization of volunteer service programs, administered locally and coordinated nationally by DHS, which seek to mitigate disasters and prepare the population for emergency response through public education, training, and outreach. Most <a href="/wiki/Disaster_response" title="Disaster response">disaster response</a> is carried out by volunteer organizations. In the US, the <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">Red Cross</a> is chartered by Congress to coordinate disaster response services. It is typically the lead agency handling shelter and feeding of evacuees. Religious organizations, with their ability to provide volunteers quickly, are usually integral during the response process. The largest being the <a href="/wiki/Salvation_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvation Army">Salvation Army</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> with a primary focus on chaplaincy and rebuilding, and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptists" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Baptists">Southern Baptists</a> who focus on food preparation and distribution,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> as well as cleaning up after floods and fires, chaplaincy, mobile shower units, chainsaw crews and more. With over 65,000 trained volunteers, Southern Baptist Disaster Relief is one of the largest disaster relief organizations in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Similar services are also provided by Methodist Relief Services, the Lutherans, and <a href="/wiki/Samaritan%27s_Purse" title="Samaritan\'s Purse">Samaritan\'s Purse</a>. Unaffiliated volunteers show up at most large disasters. To prevent abuse by criminals, and for the safety of the volunteers, procedures have been implemented within most response agencies to manage and effectively use these \'SUVs\' (<a href="/wiki/Spontaneous_Unaffiliated_Volunteers" title="Spontaneous Unaffiliated Volunteers">Spontaneous Unaffiliated Volunteers</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The US Congress established the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Excellence_in_Disaster_Management_and_Humanitarian_Assistance" title="Center for Excellence in Disaster Management and Humanitarian Assistance">Center for Excellence in Disaster Management and Humanitarian Assistance</a> (COE) as the principal agency to promote disaster preparedness in the Asia-Pacific region.</p>\n<p>The National Tribal Emergency Management Council (NEMC) is a non-profit educational organization developed for Tribal organizations to share information and best practices, as well as to discuss issues regarding public health and safety, emergency management and homeland security, affecting those under Indian sovereignty. NTMC is organized into Regions, based on the FEMA 10 region system. NTMC was founded by the Northwest Tribal Emergency Management Council (NWTEMC), a consortium of 29 Tribal Nations and Villages in Washington, Idaho, Oregon, and Alaska.</p>\n<p>If a disaster or emergency is declared to be terror related or an "Incident of National Significance," the Secretary of Homeland Security will initiate the <a href="/wiki/National_Response_Framework" title="National Response Framework">National Response Framework</a> (NRF). The NRF allows the integration of federal resources with local, country, state, or tribal entities, with management of those resources to be handled at the lowest possible level, utilizing the <a href="/wiki/National_Incident_Management_System" title="National Incident Management System">National Incident Management System</a> (NIMS).</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a> offer <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.emergency.cdc.gov/hazards-specific.asp">information</a> for specific types of emergencies, such as disease outbreaks, natural disasters and severe weather, chemical and radiation accidents, etc. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cdc.gov/niosh/emres/">Emergency Preparedness and Response Program</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Occupational_Safety_and_Health" title="National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health">National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health</a> develops resources to address responder safety and health during responder and recovery operations.</p>\n<h4><span id="FEMA\'s_Emergency_Management_Institute"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="FEMA.27s_Emergency_Management_Institute">FEMA\'s Emergency Management Institute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: FEMA\'s Emergency Management Institute">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Management_Institute" title="Emergency Management Institute">Emergency Management Institute</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_7740_-_Photograph_by_Jocelyn_Augustino_taken_on_03-10-2003_in_Maryland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/FEMA_-_7740_-_Photograph_by_Jocelyn_Augustino_taken_on_03-10-2003_in_Maryland.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_7740_-_Photograph_by_Jocelyn_Augustino_taken_on_03-10-2003_in_Maryland.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/FEMA_-_7740_-_Photograph_by_Jocelyn_Augustino_taken_on_03-10-2003_in_Maryland.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_7740_-_Photograph_by_Jocelyn_Augustino_taken_on_03-10-2003_in_Maryland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/FEMA_-_7740_-_Photograph_by_Jocelyn_Augustino_taken_on_03-10-2003_in_Maryland.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_7740_-_Photograph_by_Jocelyn_Augustino_taken_on_03-10-2003_in_Maryland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="722" data-file-height="470" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_7740_-_Photograph_by_Jocelyn_Augustino_taken_on_03-10-2003_in_Maryland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Emergency_Management_Institute" title="Emergency Management Institute">Emergency Management Institute</a>\'s Main Campus in <a href="/wiki/Emmitsburg,_Maryland" title="Emmitsburg, Maryland">Emmitsburg, Maryland</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Emergency Management Institute (EMI) serves as the national focal point for the development and delivery of emergency management <a href="/wiki/Training" title="Training">training</a> to enhance the capabilities of <a href="/wiki/State_government" title="State government">state</a>, territorial, <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">local</a>, and tribal government officials; volunteer organizations; FEMA\'s disaster workforce; other Federal agencies; and the public and private sectors to minimize the impact of disasters and <a href="/wiki/Emergency" title="Emergency">emergencies</a> on the American public. EMI curricula are structured to meet the needs of this diverse audience with an emphasis on separate organizations working together in all-hazards emergencies to save lives and protect property. Particular emphasis is placed on governing doctrine such as the <a href="/wiki/National_Response_Framework" title="National Response Framework">National Response Framework</a> (NRF), <a href="/wiki/National_Incident_Management_System" title="National Incident Management System">National Incident Management System</a> (NIMS), and the National Preparedness Guidelines.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> EMI is fully accredited by the International Association for Continuing Education and Training (IACET) and the <a href="/wiki/American_Council_on_Education" title="American Council on Education">American Council on Education</a> (ACE).<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Approximately 5,500 participants attend resident courses each year while 100,000 individuals participate in non-resident programs sponsored by EMI and conducted locally by state emergency management agencies under cooperative agreements with FEMA. Another 150,000 individuals participate in EMI-supported exercises, and approximately 1,000 individuals participate in the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Stockpile_Emergency_Preparedness_Program" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemical Stockpile Emergency Preparedness Program">Chemical Stockpile Emergency Preparedness Program</a> (CSEPP).<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <i>independent study</i> program at EMI consists of free courses offered to United States citizens in <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Emergency_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="Comprehensive Emergency Management">Comprehensive Emergency Management</a> techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Course IS-1 is entitled "Emergency Manager: An Orientation to the Position" and provides background information on FEMA and the role of emergency managers in agency and volunteer organization coordination. The EMI Independent Study (IS) Program, a Web-based distance learning program open to the public, delivers extensive online training with approximately 200 courses. It has trained more than 2.8 million individuals. The EMI IS Web site receives 2.5 to 3 million visitors a day.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span id="SMAUG_model_\xe2\x80\x93_a_basis_for_prioritizing_hazard_risks"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="SMAUG_model_.E2.80.93_a_basis_for_prioritizing_hazard_risks">SMAUG model \xe2\x80\x93 a basis for prioritizing hazard risks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: SMAUG model \xe2\x80\x93 a basis for prioritizing hazard risks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In emergency or <a href="/wiki/Disaster_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Disaster management">disaster management</a> the SMAUG model of identifying and prioritizing risk of hazards associated with natural and technological threats is an effective tool. SMAUG stands for Seriousness, Manageability, Acceptability, Urgency and Growth and are the criteria used for prioritization of hazard risks. The SMAUG model provides an effective means of prioritizing hazard risks based upon the aforementioned criteria in order to address the risks posed by the hazards to the avail of effecting effective <a href="/w/index.php?title=Risk_mitigation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Risk mitigation (page does not exist)">mitigation</a>, reduction, response and <a href="/wiki/Disaster_recovery" title="Disaster recovery">recovery</a> methods.<sup id="cite_ref-AnnexB_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnnexB-122">[122]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Seriousness can be defined as "The relative impact in terms of people and dollars." This includes the potential for lives to be lost and potential for injury as well as the physical, social and as mentioned, economic losses that may be incurred</p>\n<p>Manageability can be defined as "the relative ability to mitigate or reduce the hazard (through managing the hazard, or the community or both)". Hazards presenting a high risk and as such requiring significant amounts of risk reduction initiatives will be rated high.<sup id="cite_ref-AnnexB_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnnexB-122">[122]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Acceptability - The degree to which the risk of hazard is acceptable in terms of political, environmental, social and economic impact</p>\n<p>Urgency - This is related to the probability of risk of hazard and is defined in terms of how imperative it is to address the hazard <sup id="cite_ref-AnnexB_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnnexB-122">[122]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Growth - This is the potential for the hazard or event to expand or increase in either probability or risk to community or both. Should vulnerability increase, potential for growth may also increase.</p>\n<p>An example of the numerical ratings for each of the four criteria is shown below:<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tr>\n<td>Manageability</td>\n<td>High = 7+</td>\n<td>Medium = 5\xe2\x80\x937</td>\n<td>Low = 0\xe2\x80\x934</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Urgency</td>\n<td>High = &lt;20yr</td>\n<td>Medium = &gt;20yr</td>\n<td>Low = 100yrs</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Acceptability</td>\n<td>High priority - poses more significant risk</td>\n<td>low priority - Lower risk of hazard impact</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Growth</td>\n<td>High = 3</td>\n<td>Medium = 2</td>\n<td>Low = 1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Seriousness</td>\n<td>High = 4-5</td>\n<td>Medium = 2-3</td>\n<td>Low = 0-1</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Emergency_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul>\n<li>\n<ul>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.emergency.cdc.gov/hazards-specific.asp">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention\'s Information on Specific Types of Emergencies</a></li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cdc.gov/niosh/emres/">Emergency Preparedness and Response Resources</a> by the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Occupational_Safety_and_Health" title="National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health">National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health</a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Disaster_response" title="Disaster response">Disaster Response</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Disaster_medicine" title="Disaster medicine">Disaster medicine</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Emergency_Communication_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Emergency Communication System">Emergency Communication System</a></li>\n<li><a Fronti\xc3\xa8res">M\xc3\xa9decins Sans Fronti\xc3\xa8res</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/NetHope" title="NetHope">NetHope</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline"
